O you, dear sons, I have completed this book for you which contains the principles and practice of the medical science, and have finished it with explanations and descriptions. And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery."
And because the practical art is forbidden in our region and is strange in all aspects, thus the science has perished and has been cut off, and nothing remains of it except for small descriptions in books by ancient authors which have been copied by hand. And from this came the errors and false beliefs, and intentions were clouded and the science was driven away.
It seems to me that I wish to compile together the organization of this treatise following the order of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will compile together the forms of the fire-making tools for cautery, as well as the other instruments of the work with the addition of explanation and preparation, as is necessary.
And because no skilled masters of handiwork are found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected. And it is necessary for one who practices (medicine) to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that he knows thoroughly about the members, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and the number of them, and their movement and repose, and where they originate.
And so Hippocrates said that a name without deeds is much, and in the art of handiwork, it is the same.
We tell you at the beginning of this book that he who is not knowledgeable about the previously mentioned things, let him beware that he does not fall into error and kill men; just as I have seen many times with those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and experience.
For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula or the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck; because of which so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone of a watery man, and the stone was large; he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
And I had already been called to operate on him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if he were operated on, he would die.
And see another physician who took in charge a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound; and the ignorant physician tightly binds the break over the wound with bandages, and leaves no salt to the wound, and binds it like this for a while; and he ordered him not to loosen it; and it remained so until the leg became completely swollen and the foot came to perdition.
I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and unbind the leg; and when I had undone it, he was at ease and did not feel any pain.
But in any case, the corruption had already spread throughout the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption continued to spread through the member until the entire limb was lost.[](Note: The word "corruption" in this context likely refers to infection or gangrene.)
And see another physician who lanced a hardened abscess, and then inflamed it further due to the malignancy of his treatment. (Note: The word "malignity" in this context may refer to the severity or virulence of the infection, or to the negative consequences of the physician's actions.)
For chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, one should not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can completely remove what is corrupt.
And so, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two branches: that is to say, surgery where there is danger in many positions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to be cautious, so that foolish fools cannot speak ill of you.
So take up your arms in silence, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that through the grace of God you come to safety and are praised; and leave behind diseases that inspire dread with serious illness; and put aside your weapons from those that make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can go from this world to the other with glory.
Galen said in one of his admonitions: "Do not take care of bad illnesses, lest you be called a foolish fool."
I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
The first chapter is about cauteries of fire and cauteries of sharp medicine, and this chapter is arranged from head to foot; and the forms of instruments, and the iron tools of cautery, and all that is necessary for the work.
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping glasses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged with the forms of instruments.
The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is arranged from head to foot, and the forms of instruments.[ST1]
So that we may remember the work, it is necessary for me to tell of the quality and the harm of each complexion.
I say that the qualities of help and harm, it is the longest word and most subtle science and secret knowledge; and of this, many sages spoke and agreed to it; and I am not satisfied with their words, for I fear lengthiness.
I say that cautery helps universally for all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, a hot complexion without matter, and a dry complexion without matter.
In a hot and dry complexion together with matter, some have divided and said that cautery is of great help; and others have said the opposite: that cautery is of no value for illnesses that come from heat and dryness.
For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to cure illnesses caused by heat and dryness; and he who says the opposite, that cautery brings great help to hot and dry illnesses in the human body, speaks falsely. For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body to be cold.
And I agree with this statement. For I have found it to be true through experience.
And yet, it should not be meddled with by anyone other than the one who has tested it and is well-versed in the chapter of cauteries, as well as the diversity of human complexions, their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and the outcomes and seasons; we are not afraid of other complexions, even cold and moist ones. And all the physicians gathered and agreed on the use of cautery.
And know, son, that fire cautery is among the treatments for curing and of greater benefit than heated medical cautery.
For fire is simple and does not spread beyond the member that is burned, and does not harm any other member unless it happens to name so.
Heated medicines spread from one member to another and bring illnesses with difficult healing to the affected member; and perhaps kill the patient.
Fire, due to its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this (spread illness) unless there is an excess.
And I have found this to be true through experience and through the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and it is based on the truth of things. And for this reason, I excuse myself for the length of my speech, for I do not wish to take away from you the secret that is hidden in fire and its quality of work, how it removes illnesses from bodies, as the philosopher says and demonstrates; now receive it in your thoughts.
And know, son, that they agreed upon a certain time for cauteries to be performed, and they chose pricking.
And I say that a cautery is appropriate in all times, because the harm arising is diminished by the aid of cautery; and even if the cauterization is necessary due to urgent and severe pain that cannot wait for the time when greater harm does not come to the limb.
And never think, dear son, as foolish men do; for the illness that is healed by cauterization does not return; and they say so; but it is not as they think, because a cautery is not a medicine that changes complexion, and dries up the humors that are the cause of pain, rather it is a means to an end that is more effective than medicine due to its swiftness of action, and the power of its work and sovereignty.
And it is possible that the illness comes at times according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the disease and its power; and excesses accumulate in him through the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered in a place where there is little excess and moisture, such as cauteries for pain, and similar things, and that type of pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
And many people do not understand why cautery is called the "derrière" (after part/hindering part) of medicine, but this is true; however, they do not believe that cautery is effective after other treatments, but their belief is false. The term "cautery is the derrière of medicine" means that when we administer methods of cures in a disease and they are not effective, we then apply cautery, and it works. Then it becomes clear that cautery is the "derrière" (after part/hindering part) of medicine, but not in the way foolish physicians think.
The ancients said that cautery with an instrument of gold is more effective than iron, and they did not say this without reason but because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance. They also said that the place of cauterization does not become necrotic, but this is not true as I have experienced. Gold cautery is indeed more effective than iron, just as they claimed.[translation varies slightly from previous answer]
And yet, when you heat an instrument of gold, you cannot tell when it is hot enough by its color, which can cool down very quickly. If it is heated too much, it becomes brittle and breaks in the fire. In this way, there are many obstacles to using gold cautery.
And so we make use of the fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
I have arranged this chapter from head to toe, so that the way may be easier to find.
of the olive cautery[^1^](#note-1)
This cautery is useful for treating moisture and coldness on the brain, and there are two types of it used for a condition called "soda," as well as for various humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, causing many dreams, toothaches, sore throats, and all illnesses that result from coldness, such as paralysis, numbness, apoplexy, and similar conditions.
The shape of this cautery is such that the patient must be purged with a cleansing medicine that clears the head three or four times, depending on the patient's vitality, fluids, and habits; and then let the patient's head sweat.[^1^](#note-2)
And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on something firm; then place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his two eyes; and where your middle fingers come, bleed slightly, then heat the cautery called "olivary," of which this is the shape:
And place it on the marked spot with ink, and make downward and outward movements while pulling your hand back and forth; then quickly remove your hand, and check the mark to see if you see a small hole; and if you do not see it, reapply the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; then take a little bit of salt, put it in wine and soft cotton, and place it on the mark, and let it stay for three days; then put dampened linen cloths with butter on top; and leave it on until the burn has healed; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrapharmacum" until it is healed.
And the ancients said that the longer a wound stays open, the more it purges itself; and for this reason, movement helps.
And some of them said that one should leave the cautery on long enough that part of the bone is burnt, and then scrape off what has been burnt from the bone and have it treated.[](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caut%C3%A8re)
And they say that one should leave the cautery for a while, and apply it strongly enough that it makes a wound as large as a distaff that women place in their spindles so that the humors may exit; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one should clean and close it.
And these two methods of cauterization do not seem good to me in every way, except in certain men where there is fear; and it seems to me that I should leave out the other one; for the head is weakened by continuous natural evacuations, as we observe in other members; and even when the head of the patient is naturally weak, and the first appearance of cauterization is more healthy and effective for me, I use this one and achieve a positive outcome.
of the old pain in the head
When there is chronic pain coming all over the head and lasting a long time, then the patient should use herbs and pills which are called "cochie", and purgatives for the head and oil treatments and poultices; and if one does cauterization as we have previously mentioned, but it is not effective.
Take care if the patient's condition is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold; then cauterize beneath the fire cautery a little as we have said above.
Afterward, make a cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery or incision in the place called "vasselz"; and it is an incision where one applies cupping glasses; and lighten your hand so that you do not see all the way to the bone: the patient feels much more severe pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of this later; and the cauteries of the horns should be finer than those used for the middle of the head, and this is the method.
of the head cautery When sudden pain comes to a part of the head and the illness extends up to the eye, and the head has been purged with cleansing medicines, and the other cures that I have said in the division of diseases have been done, and all this does not help; then one should make cauteries in two ways: namely by means of medicine and by fire.
The medical procedure of the cautery in medicine is as follows: take a piece of aloe wood, remove the bark, and cut it into a piece to fit two fingers. Then make an incision where the pain lies, in such a way that you can place the piece of aloe wood underneath the skin; and when it is placed, bind and tighten it well, leaving it in place for twelve hours; then unbind it and remove the piece of aloe, and leave the wound open for two or three days; then apply a compress soaked in butter until it heals.
After the treatment of ointment until it is healed; and if you wish, apply any of the burning medicines that I have written about in the twelfth chapter on burning medicines.
The iron cautery is in the following manner. Heat the cautery to the shape depicted here:
And it is called "clos" because the end is shaped like a bell with one hollowed-out curve and a small opening in the middle. Place it on the painful area and move your hand holding the iron cautery gently until half of its thickness has been burnt; then remove your hand so that the artery, which is outside and beyond, does not get burnt, allowing for the abundant flow of blood.
Afterwards, put cotton at the wound covered with silk, and leave it for 3 days; then put wet cotton smeared with butter, and then cure the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this swelling with the cautery called "cultellare", do it at the entire tip, and take care not to cover the artery in this swelling which is not old.
The term "emigraine" from the original Old French text likely refers to a type of swelling or tumor. In modern medical terminology, it could be translated as "swelling", "tumor", or "growth". However, without further context, it is difficult to provide an exact translation.
When you cure a swelling (emigraine) as we have said before in the section on diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the previous cautery of medicine and iron is not sufficient, then you should heat the "cultellare" cautery until it is white. And similarly place it on the painful spot, drawing a line half a finger long, and remove your hand once, and pull so as not to cover the artery and reach the bone; and beware of the jaw that moves when chewing, and see that the nerve does not move and that spasm does not come upon the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut or if there is great fear in both the one who knows it and the one who does not know it, and who is not a student and experienced. And leave the work half-done; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it belongs in this book.
And if you see that these cauteries are not sufficient for the disease and the patient is willing, then cauterize it in the same place on the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the previous one and more helpful.
of the pain of the ears from part coldness
When pain comes to the ear from coldness, and medical treatments and other cures as we have mentioned in the division have been attempted but the pain persists, then heat this "pointed" cautery, which has the following form:
After, apply the cautery all around the affected ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move it slightly above the root of the ear after you have marked the spot; and make ten cautery marks around each ear; then cure the area until it is healed.
of the torture of the mouth[Written during a time when medical terminology used language that would now be considered harsh or inappropriate.]
Torture of the mouth that should be cured by cautery is only one of those that move fluids, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make cautery for similar ones that come from dryness and nerve spasms.[Written during a time when medical terminology used language that would now be considered harsh or inappropriate.].
When you treat this type of torture that moves with fluid from sweating, cleansing of the head and gargling, and if it is ineffective, then you should cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the base of the ear, another a little behind the temple, and the third on the joint of the two lips; and place the cautery on the healthy-looking part, and make the cautery next to the head of the ear slightly below the ear horn, and another on the temple as long as a thumb; and leave the cautery in place until half of the heart is burnt; and this is the form of the cautery.
And this is the appearance of the scalpel that we mentioned before, but it is slightly more subtle and requires that the knife be a little larger; after treating the wound as I said before, until it heals completely.
When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one at the top of the head, and one in the place called "vasselz" as we mentioned before, and the last cautery on the stomach; and treat it as we have said before.
The term "litargie" is a medieval medical term used to describe a condition characterized by vertigo or dizziness. It is derived from the Latin word "lithargyros," which means "calcareous," and was used in ancient times to refer to a type of lead carbonate that was believed to cause vertigo when ingested. In medieval medical texts, litargie often refers to a condition characterized by dizziness, disorientation, or difficulty with balance. The term may be used to describe a variety of conditions that can cause these symptoms, including inner ear disorders, neurological problems, or certain medications.
For this ailment, give the patient large y ears and cleansing pills for the brain; afterward, raise the patient's head and apply to the back of the head the plaster of sinapis (mustard) that is written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the method of cautery: do it as I have said.
If it (the patient) is healed in this way, that is good; and if not, perform three cauteries on the head, starting at the top and going down to the neck, leaving a space of two fingers between each cautery; and treat it as you would any other injury, adding to it if necessary, and if the patient is tolerant, perform one cautery in the middle; and if needed, two others on the two temples, and continue treating until it is healed; and let the cautery used be called "olivare," as I have mentioned before.
of the coolness/coldness of the head The head must be cleansed of hairs and other things as we have mentioned before; then raise the patient's head and perform cautery on the head and on each temple, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is tolerant, and the ailment is severe, then perform four cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave it until the outermost part of the burn has healed, then remove your hand; then treat it until it is healed, and use the "olivare" cautery that we mentioned before.
of epilepsy
Epileptics should not use fire cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to cleanse the brain of yeers and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and able to take medicine.
And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, have them gargle and chew food that will cleanse the brain often with wholesome meats; then anoint the head in the middle, and perform one cautery on the vessel, and one on each horn; and if the patient is strong and able to tolerate it, perform cauteries as I have said for someone who has paralysis and weakening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterizations be with olive oil in the manner that I have said.
If the patient is a child, perform one subtle cautery in this manner:
When, due to melancholy, superfluidities or corrupt moistures and thick phlegm are present, then use such cauteries as we have said for someone suffering from paralysis.
And if, due to melancholy, superfluities decline towards melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that will purify the brain, as specified in the previously mentioned division.
After that, wash the patient's head; then make a well-made linen compress, like a circle, and place it on their head; have the patient lie crosswise, and be well held in all ways; then present the liniment, and warm it with aged butter; and heat it over moderate fire, so that the forehead can tolerate it; then empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week with other good care, until they are healed.
If you wish to cauterize by making multiple points across the entire cautery, this method of cauterization moistens the brain excessively; and then place wet cotton in butter and chicken fat on top.
of the inflammation of the eyes When inflammation comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink something cleansing for the head, and guard against all moisture, and make them sweat or take baths several times while fasting.
Afterwards, instruct them to tilt their head back, and perform cautery in the middle of the forehead, and make two cauterizations on the temples if the spread of inflammation is in both eyes together or in one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are under the skull with the cautery, and let the cauterization be long according to the width of the temple; and watch for excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it as best you can.
And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision how to stretch it carefully, and sometimes a cautery or hot iron is made under the two bones at the back.
the heart of tears
When the tears of the eyes have become old and customary and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are apparent on the outside of the head; and one sees that it is due to cold fluids, then he should apply the cautery that I mentioned in the beginning of the chapter, descending toward the eyes: one cautery on the forehead, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries at the haiterel below the two bones; and if there is need for more, then cauterize abundantly above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
of the fluid inside the eyes.
When you administer the medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient three cups of cooked wine; raise his head, and apply the middle-sized cautery on the crown of the head, and make two cauteries with the "clavilis" cautery on the two eyebrows, a little below the hairline; and be careful not to cover the artery. And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis".
When the papyrus of the eye is made soft by disease and moisture, then use this cautery which is called "olivary," of which the form is as follows:
And if you wish to do so, make two cauteries on the two swellings as long as they are; and do not remove your hand until a third part of the papyrus is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
the hair that pricks the eye Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and then cauteries are made in two ways: namely with fire or with a heated medical substance.
For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
When they (hair) grow out evenly, place the patient in your care; then on paper place a shape that is similar to the leaf of a fern, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; next put cotton soaked in egg white and powdered parsley on the eye, then heat the cautery to the shape shown here:
After cauterizing along the shape that you have marked many times, so that the skin is burnt evenly; and the sign of the success of the procedure is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs lifted at the edge of the eye; then lift your hand and leave it like that for three days, then apply moist cotton in butter until the burn is healed; after that treat with ointment until it has healed.
And if after this the hairs return and the paper becomes softened, then resume cauterizing in that same spot as before; and if the hairs are missing, cauterize until the paper rises to its natural position, is even, and the hairs no longer prick the eye.
The burning medical cautery is what you command the patient to let their hairs grow long and even; then make a parchment in the shape of a fern leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one third, and grind them well together; and do it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread it on the shape you have made like the fern leaf, and put it on the paper of the eyes; and if the illness is in one eye only, then work on one, and if in both as well; and place wet cotton under the eye with egg white; and the patient's head should be in your care and place your hand showing above the medicine, and press a little and move it every time the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for they feel biting as if by fire. When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from the wound. And when the biting (of the cautery) has passed, remove the cauterizing iron and check if you see the skin lifted as if it had been lifted by constriction of fire or incision; and if it is so, then it is good. If not, apply more medicine to the area where the medicine has not yet worked, until your work is even and your eyes are healed; then place a wet cotton compress soaked in butter on the burnt area until the burn has healed; after that, cure the wound with an ointment called "diaphoretic" and other remedies until it is healed.
And if you need to be careful in your work, take great care that the medicine does not get into the eyes. If the skin becomes soft and the hairs prick the eye, then reapply the medicine to the affected area properly, just as you did before; after that, cure it until it is healed; and this is the method of treating a burn:
And know that the eyes of humans are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this, your constriction (of the eye) should be adjusted; and do not apply the same method to those who study this art (as you would to others), meaning that you should adjust your technique accordingly based on each individual's unique anatomy.
of the treatment of fistula by cautery
When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then it is necessary to apply cautery to it in this manner.
Command the patient to place their head in your lap; and hold the patient's head between your hands so that it does not move or shift; then apply a cotton swab soaked in egg white or parsley juice on the eye; then heat the cautery tool which is parted: and place it on the head like the shape of a dove's feather quill, bring the two parts together while heating; if you wish, sharpen it from one end to the other, and if you wish, make it rounded like a tent; but in any case, this tool will be useful for your work.
Afterwards, press on the fistula if it is open, and remove the pus and the dry matter; and if it is closed, operate on it and remove the blockage; then place hot wheat flour on the cautery, and hold your hand on the cautery at the white part above the eye, so that your hand does not move excessively; and place the cautery in the oil of the eye, and corrode (burn) it.
If you come to the beginning of the cauterization to the bone, it would be good. If not, then repeat the cautery once more, and another time if necessary, and leave it for three days; then apply a cotton swab soaked in butter, and treat the wound with a drying ointment until it is healed; and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then apply a corrosive medicine to uncover the bone; and the king according to what comes up in his chapter (instructions).
And there is a kind of fire cautery for fistula that some of the ancients mentioned. Understand "fistula," and open the location; then place in the opening a thin piece of iron, the shape of which is as follows: And they make it to the size of a hazelnut; and hold your hand firmly on the iron, and let the patient not move at all, lest the molten lead run into their eye; and you must place over the patient's eye cotton soaked in egg white or oil: the lead will draw out the pus from the fistula, and the healthy flesh will heal miraculously.
And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good. If not, then one must administer a perforation to the new growth and bring the fistula back to the body of the new growth as it should be in its proper place.[∎](Note: The above translations are provided in plain text format without any additional comments or contextual information.)
It appears that the given phrase is in Modern French and not Old French. The translation of "des crevasses en lèvres" to English is "cracks in lips". Much oftentimes, cracks appear on lips that are called "wrinkles," and likewise on the lips of children.
When you treat these cracks, as we have said in divisions, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small scalpel-like cautery of this form:
And quickly place it in the cracks until it reaches the root; after that, cover the area with a salve until it is healed.
of an abscess in the throat
When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or the eye, or the palate, or the roots of the teeth, after it putrefies and rots and becomes enfeebled and turns into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not help at all: then you must have a cautery of the size of the fistula; place it on the opening or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches the bottom of it, and the surrounding area; and do this once or twice, after the treatment of what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is treated in this way, it is good; but if not, then you must reveal the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
from movement of the teeth
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicine but it is of no avail, then place the patient's head in your lap; after that, heat the cautery so that its shape conforms to the following manner: place a stick on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery inside, holding your hand so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and repeat the cautery as you desire; afterwards, have the patient fill their mouth with salt water and hold it for an hour and then spit it out.
And in this manner, the moving tooth is strengthened, and the softened gum is constrained, and the moisture corrupted and dried out.
of toothache
When toothache comes from cold or there is cold in the area and medical treatment does not work, then it is necessary to use cautery in two ways: with butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautery of butter is as follows: take cow's butter, and the tip in an iron or bronze ladle; then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a lance, and soak it in boiled butter, and put it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it there until it has cooled down; and do this frequently until the power/strength reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see it necessary, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the painful tooth, and place a hot iron on it until the heat reaches the tooth's nerve.
The fire cautery is as follows: take an iron or bronze rod, and make it thick enough so that the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, which will form as follows, and place it on the tooth, holding your hand until the cautery has cooled down; do this frequently, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next. And it is necessary for the patient to fill their mouth with good butter in preparation for this cautery, and then rinse it out; and this is the form of the cautery:
When the scrofulous swellings are of phlegm and of cold moistures, and are not responsive to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery with a substance whose form comes after, and have two openings for the fumes to escape on the side of the cautery; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to its size, and leave it in place for three days; and place a wet cotton soaked in butter where the burn is, until the burn is healed; after that, treat the area with ointments and bandages until it is healed.

of fungi that come to the feet
It often happens that on the feet there arises an illness which is called "clos" in our language, and it is a large abscess that wounds the foot. Do this one after another, until you reach all those on the body, then cure them with ointments that generate flesh.

of foul pustules

when an artery is cut Often there are heavy bleedings of blood from the cut artery that spread outward, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cauterization of a limb, and in similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to stop the bleeding.
And yet when this happens to someone, you must quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press very hard so that the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more drips from it; then heat various olive-shaped cauters, both large and small, until they are all red; then apply one, whether large or small, according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut, and place the cauter on that vein where you have your finger and hold it there until the bleeding has stopped.
And if it starts to bleed again when you remove your finger from the vein, and the cauter is extinguished, take another one quickly from those that are in the fire.
And do not stop doing this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and make sure that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be easily stopped, especially if the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four means that we have mentioned: either with a cauter, or through extraction when it is not treated, or by tightly binding with a bandage, or with medicines applied to it that have the power to stop bleeding; and let it be bound and constricted appropriately.
Who will treat tight constriction with bandages or place hot things on it, or similar things, will not benefit much from it. (My translation)
And if this happens to anyone who does not have any remedy or medicine present, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it out until it is tightened over the wound and the vein; and must not move it, but moisten it frequently with very cold water until the blood is congealed and swollen and tightened; and make preparations for what they need in terms of cautery and medicine.
We have told you in the first chapter all diseases for which it is necessary to use fire cautery or a hot medicine, and we have described the instruments and forms of cauteries; and I have arranged this chapter from head to toe, and in this chapter, I will proceed in the same manner so that one can more easily find what they are looking for.
And so, as I begin this, it is appropriate, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
And I advise you not to undertake foolish things. For many kinds of people come for cures, some of whom are so afraid of their illness that they easily die from the violence they find in their disease and the severity of its harm; and these should be feared. And among these there are those who regain their strength and say: "wait, I am healed"; but the illness is contemptuous. One should by no means agree to those who come to you with this attitude, but rather place greater emphasis on your honor than on your greed, and do not foolishly open up for those about whom you are uncertain and from whom you cannot gain both profit and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the care of your patients so that health may be restored; and this will help you to establish a good reputation, and glory, and a memory of praise.
Dear son, may Our Lord give you understanding and correctness, and if you wish to inspire of the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
I have divided this chapter into sections for you, as it is in the chapter on cauteries that I have previously described, from head to toe, so that you may more easily find what you need.
a head full of water
Know that this illness often occurs in children during childbirth, and when the birth is difficult and the mother squeezes the child's head too hard; and sometimes it happens for no apparent reason.
And I never saw this disease except in children, and in all those that I have seen, death came quickly; and for this reason, it seems better to me to abandon the treatment in such cases.
And I saw a child where the head was full of water, and the neck swelled each day so that it could no longer support itself; and the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture is collected under the skin on the neck between the throat and the bone; and the treatment is such if the moisture is between the throat and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make an incision in the middle of the neck a finger's width long; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture can run out; and behold the shape of the spatula:
If the moisture is more swollen and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the signs that the corners of the mouth are open on both sides, and the water jumps out when you press it from the inside with your hand, and this does not heal; then you must make three incisions in the middle of the neck in this manner:
And after the incision, remove all pus; Afterward, bind the wounds with cloth and powder, and apply wine and oil, and leave it like this until the fifth day; then undo the binding, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and continue to bind the head as well, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
And another way of incision is to look where the swelling of the abscess is most prominent and where the water has gathered; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Incise then where the abscess is most prominent and where the water has gathered, and make an incision according to what you have the power to do; and be careful not to cut an artery; and if a flow of blood comes, so that the patient dies from bleeding and evacuation of pus.

Therefore, when you burn the eyes, it is necessary that the patient bend their head back; after that, rub the area around it with a rough cloth until the arteries appear; then have the patient stretch out their neck with one cloth; then look for where the veins bulge, and they are located one on each side of the ears, and are slightly sunken; then mark the spots with ink; then burn one and the other with a sharp spatula in two parts until the incision reaches the bone, and this should be done across the forehead.

Of tears.
When the tears are flowing from the veins that are above the forehead and no medicine helps, and you see the face of the patient become red, and feel a pulsation on the forehead like a trembling; and if the eyelids are tight and moist so that the paper has fallen off, and the papers have been warmed up and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this remedy is required. from the incision at the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the flesh that is between the two cuts right up to the sinciput (scalp tissue) above the bone. Then do the same thing from the middle incision to the other second one, after which extract this mixture.

of the swelling of the eyes
When someone is accustomed to getting a catarrh, and you see the eyes sunken and small, with weakened vision, and inflamed eyelids; and the hair falls out, and there is deep pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know by these signs that those matters and those catarrhs do not come from one vein alone, and the proper cure for it is this.
And it is necessary for you to instruct the patient to bend their forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one about an inch wide. Begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let it reach the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move while eating; once the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two lips of the incision and place a piece of old cotton, and bandage with linen cloth; then apply dampened bandages on it with wine and oil, and be careful not to cause a hot abscess; once removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents that help the flesh to heal.
In this manner: take 2 parts of wheat flour and 4 parts of colophony, and make it into an ointment; and apply it to these wounds to help the flesh grow throughout.
of stuffing the ears
All that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains or an animal or a stone from mines or similar things such as iron; or seed such as lice, beans, peas; or fluid such as water and mucus and similar things.
When something falls into the ear such as a stone or any other thing that does not fit well in the ear or grow in the ear, then expose the ear to sunlight. If you see the stone, apply a few drops of violet oil or wormseed oil, then facilitate extraction; make them sneeze using condiments, and block their nostrils when they sneeze, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and pull upwards on the ear. This cure often works; and if it does not work, use subtle forceps, of which this is the shape:
If it jumps out with the forceps, that's good; if not, then facilitate extraction using a fine hook made of thin double-wire; and if it does not come out this way, then make a small silver tube and insert one end into the ear canal, stopping up the area around the tube with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the tube; then pull strongly, because often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, then take birdlime, place some on an instrument suitable for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around it; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out. And if it [the abscess] does not come to a head with all the things we have mentioned, then hurry to lance the ear so that pus and swelling may come out, and the manner of lancing is as follows: first make the patient recline, then bleed them from the head, drawing blood according to their strength. Then have the patient sit between your hands, turn their ear upward, and make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fatty area; let the incision be crescent-shaped, continuing until you reach the bone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck out the pus with your mouth; treat it until it is healed. And if it is a hard grain that has formed and it swells, then perform an extraction; and if it cannot come out, then apply a thin suppository of this form:
and make an incision of that grain. But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to moisture in the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then carefully extract it with tweezers and suck it out gently, as we have said, so that the extraction may be easy.
In the case of water that falls into the ear, the patient should use expectoration with mild condiments first, and fill the ear with cotton. Let them lie on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out by this means, that is good. If not, then take many small and light pebbles, heat them slightly in the fire, and place one or two of them in the patient's ear canal and jump up and down on one foot while striking the outside of the ear with another stone. Continue to do this until all of the water has come out, and then it will be completely removed. And if you wish, take a reed and insert one end into the ear, lighting the other end on fire until the inner part is burned; repeat this process with other pieces of reed until all of the water has come out, as we have said in the previous method with stones.[Original text has some inconsistencies and repetitions which have been maintained in translation for accuracy.].
In the extraction of an animal, if it is of small size, such as a louse and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size that can be felt, then arrange for a gradual extraction with tweezers; and this is one of the easier things to remove that can be in the ear.
In the extraction of worms in the ear, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in the section on distillations, and the treatment does not work, then look at the ear in the sunlight: if you see any worms, remove them with fine tweezers, and if you don't see any, take a piece of straw such as this (...);
And make it narrow below and wide above. Insert the thinnest end of the straw into the ear according to the severity of the patient's discomfort, then pull the entire straw out; do this frequently until all the worms come out. If they don't obey by coming out, plug the straw with cotton as I have said in the section on stones; and if they still don't come out as we have described, administer the distillations that have been proven effective in the elimination of worms, which you can find in the section on distillations; and then drip your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, such as this (...).
And let it be made of silver or brass, narrow below with a small hole, and wide at the top for distillation; and have a well-made brass instrument to press the distillation inside, and if you want, take a funnel and wrap cotton around the tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you wish of your medicines into the straw, which should be in the ear; then insert the funnel with all the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or flows from the ear; and let the patient smell it inside, and let the distillation be a small bag heated by fire so that it can be distilled into the ear; and make sure that it's not too cold, as the medicine would not be effective.
of the stopping up of the ears
No child is born who does not have any holes in the ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to stopping up of wounds or pus inside the ear, and these stoppings occur sometimes deep within the ear, so that they cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small pocket at the entrance of the hole, and it can be seen.
The one that occurs deep within and cannot be seen is of difficult healing in many cases, and for the one that can be seen, you should place the ear of the patient towards the sun; and look inside: if you see an apparent blockage, then work on it using this method:
And let it be sharp and blunt both in front and behind, so that it does not wound the ear; if the blockage is due to pus or flesh in the ear, then hold it with fine tweezers and gently squeeze, until all the flesh is removed.
And if the blockage is deep within the ear, then take a fine and sharp razor, heat it slightly by fire, and place it in the ear canal. If you feel the blockage, which causes discomfort to the patient upon hearing, make a small incision but be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a wick according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.[1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian_ointment)
Do this for some days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and soak it in rose water, and powder of vitriol ground up; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you draw the tent and apply another tent soaked in cerote made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.
And if bleeding comes, soak a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
of the flesh of the papers (not sure of this translation, it could mean "pulp from paper" based on context)
This althelu (comfrey) that comes in papers for the eyes when they are moist and dry, you must stretch them with tongs and forceps, and cut off a piece of its roots with a spatula; then put vitriol powder on the spot.
And if it is not cut out, cauterize it with a subtle circular cautery, and after the incision, the cauterizer must move; and they often heal, as long as something remains of their roots; and when they are burned by fire, those roots are burnt and do not return at all.
Of hail or a hailstone.
Many times there come on paper from the eyes things that resemble hail in their shape and hardness, and for this reason, this illness is called "gravel" (or literally "hail"), and it is a gathering of thick moisture in the paper above and below; the treatment is as follows: take care if the gravel moves from one side to another, and this is easy to notice; then make an incision on each side, then gently scrape each part, then take it with forceps and cut it. If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, do not worry about the patient; and if the wound is large, sew it up with a stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do not apply any pressure, because ointments quickly restore it and improve the flesh.
And if the gravel is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper and hold the gravel with forceps, and cut it and press it from one side and the other; and if the paper is separated by incision, do not worry about it; and once the gravel has been removed, rinse the eye with salty water, and cure the wound of anything that harms the flesh until the patient heals.
of the fat of the eyes
Exinach is a fat that is instilled on paper sheets and this happens more in children than in any other people, and it greatly harms their eyes, and they have discharge in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because their tears rush to their eyes; and therefore, they lie down on their faces and sleep on it, and their papers are moist under their eyebrows which swell and have the appearance of exinach which is visible in the eye. And when you press the area around it with your fingers, you can feel the exinach coming out.
And the method of the procedure is as follows: the patient places their head over your sanctioned area; and then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach present in each part, then place it on top; and press with your fingers from one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered into the center; then make an incision in the middle of the wet area with a spatula-shaped instrument, and it should not be any larger than the wound made when opening a vein; and cut through the skin until you reach the exinach; and in multiple ways, exinach comes out of the incision, in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Then pull out all of it with a piece of cloth between your fingers and turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed; and be careful not to press too hard on the incision, not to reach the whole spatula-shaped instrument to the eye, so that you do not wound it.
And if the incision does not appear at the beginning of the cut, slightly increase the cut lengthwise until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten bandages in oil and water, and place them on the wound, and bind it with strips.
And if there are such men who crush soil and place it on (the wound) to corrupt the moisture that has remained, then cure it until it is healed. And if a hot abscess comes to the surface, then cure it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
of the hairs of the paper (shavings)
When paper shavings other than those which are natural are born, and they become ingrown and reach the eyes, they harm the eyes and bring about various types of illnesses such as watery eyes and swelling of the eyelids and cloudiness, to the point where it is the cause of eye destruction. And the cure for this is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by medicine which is appropriate according to what is before the chapter on cautery, and is done either by incision and suture or by caustics, according to what I will say.
You should place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye towards your left hand; if it is turned, that is good; if not, insert a needle with a single thread attached; and let this be beside the edge of the paper where the hairs grow next to the lashes, and pull the thread over the entire paper, and turn it to the cutter; then make an incision beneath the paper, close to the eyelashes, the entire width of the eye, from the outer canthus to the inner canthus; then remove the thread and place a small cotton and linen tent underneath the paper, then place a figure of a prop, such as a myrtle leaf, and in any case it is necessary that the figure matches the height you intend to raise the paper which is determined.
And if there is need to cut a large portion of the eyelid according to how soft the eyelid is; then make an incision the entire width of the eye along the two lines that you have marked, and begin at the outer canthus and continue to the inner canthus; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural lashes, as thick as a root, then insert the needle into one of the angles of the eyelid, then remove the skin; then bring together the two edges with a stitch of a needle with one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and apply some sticky substances to the excess threads on the eyebrows if you wish to do so; and if not, then pay it no mind, then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without stitches using drying and constricting substances, for the eyelid will heal on its own at the site of the wound and bring the edges together, but stitches are harmful (as the ancients have said), and this is a fearless operation.
And there is another way: and it is that you mark the eyelid with a figure in the shape of a myrtle leaf, as we have described, with three incisions unseparated according to the form which is shown here:
Then cut away what is above with small forceps according to the form which is shown here:
And if you do not have the strength to hold the pincers, and the thing is not even, take a needle with a thread, and place it in the middle of the wound; and put another thread next to the large lip, and the second thread next to the small one, and align the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin that you have marked, as we have told; then bring the two lips of the wound together with stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with a plaster and similar calming ointment.
And it sometimes happens that the hairs of the paper are turned inward: then you must do as we have said about the incision, but stitching in one and the other is more technical.
The treatment of veins is as follows: and it is that you turn the paper inward and make two incisions by art, and two fine ligatures as long as the paper and as wide as the width of the spatula; and cut the two ends of two parts where you hold the threads; then join them subtly on top of the part of the paper over the eye, and pull firmly the two veins from both sides; and leave it like that for several days, and the skin that is pulled will die and turn black and rot, so that it falls through it.
If it takes too long, cut deeper, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is healed, and if the paper rises up, and the hairs no longer prickle; and this is the form of the two veins that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity in length and width.
the work is such that you take a thin needle and put in it one thread of soft and thin silk; then join the edges and tie them together delicately, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then place another delicate thread of silk in the groove and tie the ends of the thread; then have the patient place his head in your lap; and be beside the sun so that the work is well-lit, for it is a delicate and fine job; then insert the needle into the entire groove at the root of the adjusted hair, and make it pierce through the paper quickly until you draw it above the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the groove, and put that hair in the groove, if there is one or two or three or more hairs; then pull your hand so that all the hairs come out at the entire groove on the paper along with the natural hair.
And if the groove is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will pull the groove from underneath the entire length of the thread that you have placed in it, until the groove comes out of the opening above and you see it with your eye; then you will pull the groove and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair hardens in its place and new skin grows over it; and if the hairs are small, then attach one long hair from natural eyebrows and lift it up with that or let it be lifted up until it is lengthened, and then tie it.
of the decay or putrefaction of the eye. The phrase "de la porriture de l'oeil" can be translated as "of the decay or putrefaction of the eye." It is not clear from the provided text how this condition relates to the instructions given, but it seems that it may be a complication or concern in the context of treating the eye.
When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the decay, comes to the eye, it can happen in two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. It can occur suddenly due to a wound, a cut, or cauterization, and similar things.
And the manner of the treatment is that you split that suture, and separate its lips, and put linen bandages in it, and bind it until it has healed; and it is not at all appropriate to use drying and constricting substances in its cure. For if you do so, the illness will return worse than before; but rather use softening substances, such as fenugreek; and let water or ale and flaxseed be cooked, and let oil-based ointments be melted in one of the oils, and wrap a bandage around it, and cure it with this.
And the treasure of your treatment is that you take care that it does not heal in the same shape as it was before; and these treatments that we have mentioned are only adjustments for this illness, so that it does not return to its former state.
of the flesh that comes into the eye
This disease that is beneath (the eye) which is truly called "axacrati", and it is both natural and accidental. The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the way to work on it is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pass from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come out in two parts of the flesh; then stretch the skin above along the entire needle, and stitch it with a spatula-shaped instrument.
And if the form of the paper returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a razor and place it in the crease, and turn the paper, and make two creases along the inside of the paper; and let the corners of the two creases be at the two angles of the incision you have made, and make them meet so that the form is like the form of a letter called "j greek"; then remove the flesh according to the amount by which its sides are uneven below the paper, then join the two separated parts and sew them together with a thread of wool; then treat it with the medicines we have mentioned, softening and bandages, until it is healed.
And if the illness comes from a wound, suture or cautery, you must make an incision in a clean line through the skin of the paper as described above; then separate between the two leaves of a bandage as I have said; and perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is diverse in form, and wise masters should prepare means with all their power to make the form return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, depending on what is required in terms of work and instruments, can adapt to multiple dispositions.
quickly of the paper
When this suture happens to many people in such a way that the paper on top is glued to the white of the eye and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the point of a razor underneath the paper and lift it up; and stretch the eyelids with forceps until you cut the very thin skin that is not raw, without being too sharp or cutting too much, so that the patient can endure it and the thin skin is not too sharp to hurt the eye. And make your incision lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and clean the whole wound, and at times put in salty water, and remove the water with sweet collyrium (a powder used as a lotion); then place a linen bandage between the paper and the eye, and place wool soaked in egg on the eye; and after three days use collyrium and other remedies until it is healed.
of the toe of the eye
Know that the cuticle (ongle) is of two kinds: one is nervous and resembles a hard callus, and another that is not nervous but rather resembles congealed white mucus, which cannot be touched with iron and pinched; and both appearances begin near the outer corner of the eye and grow little by little until they cover the entire eye and all its light and movement.
And the manner of incision is as follows: the patient places their head in your lap, then you open their eyes. Lift the paper with your hand, and use tweezers to pull the cuticle upward. Then take a needle and attach a horsehair or cow hair to it using strong thread, and insert the needle into the cuticle, piercing through completely. Attach the cuticle with thread and stretch it upwards. Then carefully remove all the hairs on the side of the cuticle that follows the eyelid and lashes up to the brow, cutting the remaining skin at the root near the outer corner of the eye using a sharp scalpel or small forceps, leaving the natural cartilage or eyebrow intact so as not to damage the tear duct. Sometimes, the cuticle extends only to the eyelash line and not beyond it, as we have mentioned; then, remove only the excess skin around the eyelashes with a soft scalpel as follows:
And be careful not to let the scalpel touch the fleshy tissue and break it, or damage the oil glands. After making the incision, put a little bit of crushed salt and collyrium (an eye medication made from antimony) into the eye, and leave it there until the next day. Then treat the eye as necessary until it is healed.
And if the nail is not sensitive, and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this similar condition of a nail is often cured with medicines; and they come to a head as I have mentioned in the division, and if you see it covered, let the patient's eye look at it, and take the spatula, not too sharp, according to this form:

The chapter on abscesses.
Many similarities of abscess are, according to what the remembrance brings afterward of one and the other in this book, and they are different in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its likeness itself, and those that hold moisture. And the second way is according to the locations where they are in the body. For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the base, and the abscesses of the fleshy part are different from those that come in joints, and each one has its judgment in the work.
And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is mature according to its development; and there are such as must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their development, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it until it is entirely rotten, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint have been corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb. Or the abscess is near the main member, and if you delay the piercing until it is matured, it will harm the main member; or it is near the base, so one must pierce it when it is dead; and one should never pierce a grown abscess without digestion being completed, except for those that are near the base, which may rot inside and elongate, causing fistula; and cannot be healed in a long time.
And it is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess when it is mature according to its development, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the softening and swelling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the incision in the lowest part of the abscess, and where it is most prominent; and let the incision be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and tendons and arteries, and all places where there is no crease.
And in those that crease, according to the member. And when the abscess is in the fleshy part, it is better to leave the incision until it is confirmed by digestion being completed, as we have said. For if you pierce it before then, the body's matter will be elongated and full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden. And there are some abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to the need of the member. And it is necessary to make small incisions in small abscesses, and small holes; and in large abscesses, large holes, and many splits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses that require cutting out the core and covering; when it has become as one cloth, and is dead, then you must do as with boils: and there are such that are cut in three angles, and such that are cut like a myrtle leaf, such as abscesses of glands; and there are such that a round incision is made, and other incisions and similar cuts.
Those who have no visible abscesses, such as a mild subcutaneous one, should be fully lanced; and when the abscess is large and has gathered great pus, you should not pull out all the pus in that hour, but instead remove some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, and remove something more; do this multiple times, increasing the amount each time, until all the pus is removed; do the same even if the patient is of weak constitution, such as women, young children, old or decrepit men. For the spirit may suddenly jump when the pus is released, causing the patient to die unexpectedly. Therefore, proceed with great caution in this matter, and once you have lanced your abscess, clean the wound and check if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a clean cut, apply bandages made of linen or old cotton; but if it is large abscesses with many holes, insert a tent into each one so that they press against each other; and if you have cut off part of the skin and pulled it back, you should fill it with old linen rags or linen cloth without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and dress the wound with ointment until it is healed.
And if bleeding occurs during your procedure, apply cold and easily absorbable water, and wet a cloth, placing it on the bleeding site multiple times. If the bleeding persists, administer treatment and care, using the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter, and the location of the abscess is very sensitive, you should place tents and damp cloths soaked in warm oil and vinegar on top; and if it is summer, and the location is fleshy, you should put damp cloths soaked in water and cold oil, or warm vinegar and oil for a whole day as we have said; then loosen the abscess, clean and dress it as required until it is healed.
And this is what should be universally understood in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one must proceed in the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.

"Des scrophules" is a term that refers to a type of abscess or swelling, usually found in the neck or jaw area. Scrofula is a form of tuberculosis that affects the lymph nodes and is characterized by the formation of painful, hard lumps under the skin. The term "scrofula" comes from the Latin word "scrofa," which means "female pig," likely because the swollen lymph nodes resemble the appearance of a pig's neck glands. In medieval medical texts like the one you provided, scrophula was often treated through various surgical procedures and the use of ointments or other topical treatments.
"Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre." This passage describes how scrophula often appears on the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin area. It also notes that they can appear elsewhere on the body and can be large and clustered together.

of the chancre

However, this phrase does not fit into the context provided by the previous sentences. Sometimes a child is born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small or not in its proper place. In such cases, it is necessary to make a tiny incision of one spatulam (a unit of measurement) with a very fine awl following this form: then insert a fine plug of linen cloth and bind and keep it in place for three or four days. When the child needs to urinate, remove the plug and allow urination, then replace the plug. It may happen that there is no need to replace the plug, since the urine coming out will not close the opening. The one whose opening is small can be treated with a linen plug as we have said, and it will widen. Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are injured, for some are born with the opening at the tip of the penis, causing them to be unable to urinate until they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the opening, and this is a bad condition.
And the method of the procedure is as follows: have the patient lie down on their back, then stretch out the head of the penis and hold it so that the opening is in the middle, as it should be; take care to avoid excessive bleeding which can occur, and if it does, stop the bleeding with a styptic and treat the wound until it heals.

of circumcision
Circumcision is not the same as loosening a continuation like other wounds; yet when we perform this work of our own volition, and particularly on children, it is necessary that we do the best and easiest work for their health.
I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, as they did not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Because I have seen that the majority of masters and healers who performed circumcision did so with a lancet around one day old, and sometimes with forceps and a scalpel; the foreskin is avoided because there are two layers to it, and by chance, the one above may be cut while leaving the one below.

It rarely happens that a stone is inserted in women, and if it happens, the cure is difficult and is forbidden by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skillful woman who reveals herself to the examiners, even when she is chaste.

And in these iron cures, there is reason to be afraid, so it is necessary to avoid them.
