then stretch out the back and cut all the skin from the haunches. then insert through the sides of the loins hooks according to what you need for opening the wound, and make them so that the intestines can exit.
then flay the siphac (urethra) which is under the skin of the haunches until the white flesh is exposed all around.[https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/siphac](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/siphac)
then insert your index finger into what follows the anus, in between the white siphac which is under the skin of the urethra, and the second siphac.
and separate what is behind the eye socket, and between the second sutures; and then move with your right hand inside the cavity of the kidneys, and stretch the white suture up to your left hand, and lift the eye socket towards the waist. and command the assistant to lift the eye socket upwards, and untie what is behind the ligament.
and feel with your hands if there is any entangled intestines or hard white suture, and if you find anything, push it down to the belly.
then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten fibers, and insert it into the back part of the suture, which is behind the kidney skin; after the waist, cut the visible threads of the fibers until there are four remaining then arrange one thread over the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the suture which is beneath the kidney skin with a strong tie made of two parts. then wrap the hips with cloths and bind them tightly from both sides, so that no vessels can reach there and cause an abscess. and then place the second bandage over the first one, which should be two digits longer than the first one, and after these two bandages, leave a space of one digit under the curve of the hips.
and then the rest following the curve like an egg carries; cut in the area under the skin of the hips, as much as necessary to let out blood and pus, as we have said before.
then apply wet wool soaked in oil, place it on the wounds and apply the bandage that we have mentioned before. And sometimes it is necessary to cauterize the white space we have mentioned after incision with caution for fear of bleeding.[I would recommend consulting a medical professional for accurate translations and interpretations of medieval medical texts as they contain outdated medical practices that are not used today.]
For this happens many times, and leave the limb until it weakens by itself; and if it delays in falling, then it should be stimulated with hot water, and place on it what we have said, until it weakens.
Then cure the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
of a carnal hernia[1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hernia#Types)
In this remedy, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the treatment using iron.
And the ancients said that it is made in such a manner as the branch that is attached to the vine, in a way that you tie the vessels, lightly above after the cut beneath;
then dip in it, and treat the abscess of whoever is working on it, until the vessels drain; and treat it as we have said, until it has healed.
Sometimes there comes a rupture in the groins, as we have said, and the opening appears; and no part of the intestines descends to the hips, and if any does descend, it is little, and it heals within hours.
However, if it remains in this state for too long, the wound or hernia grows, so much that the intestines descend.
And this happens due to the stretching of the sinew which is at the joints, as we have said, for it becomes stretched, then the place becomes softened and swollen.
And the treatment is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is treated by iron in this manner:
And it is done by having the patient lie down on their back with their affected part between your hands, then cutting the swollen area around the wound to the length of three fingers;
And then extract the sinew that is beneath the skin, then take the thread and place it on the visible surface of the wound;[
And press it deeply towards the belly, then stitch the two visible edges of the wound on the thread with a needle, and stitch both sides;[
then pull out the head of the joint, and do not cover it with a syringe or stretch the gut or any other thing, as I have made you know in the cure for dislocation of the intestines.
then heal it with the treatment of wounds. And when you bind the threads, make sure to bandage and heal the wound until it is healed.
The syringe is constricted and has no appearance in the wound, and the cautery is more useful at this place, and closer to healing.
of the softening of the skin of the buttocks.
The skin of the buttocks is often softened in some men because the flesh inside is softened, and this is visible. And when one wants to heal it, it is necessary that the patient lies on their stomach, and you cut the softened skin that is above the natural skin; then bring together the two lips with a stitch, and if you see, sew the excess of softened skin with three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and heal it like the other wounds, until it is healed, and the threads fall out.
of the surgery
Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and therefore I would not like to speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary unless for two reasons: one is that the physician may respond knowledgably when asked about it and understand the treatment; and the other is because we often have need of castrating certain animals to aid us, such as goats and sheep and pigs and other beasts. I say then that castration is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. In the one done by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles become relaxed and loose; then we pull on them with our hand until they are put back and we no longer feel them. Regarding the cutting castration: it is necessary to tie down the animal and press the skin of the scrotum with your left hand, then tie the suspending ligament and make one cut on each testicle after they have been properly skinned; and leave some of the sac around the spermatic cord and the fine spermatic cord that is above the vessels; and this method of castration is more severe than the one done by attraction, because in an attractive castration there may sometimes be a remnant of the testicles left behind, causing the animal to still have sexual desire; then clean and heal the wound until it is healed.
hermaphrodites
Hermaphrodites are of two kinds for men: one is that between the two testicles it is open like the shape of a woman's nature, where there is hair and sometimes they urinate through it. And the other kind is in women, and they have a clitoris like a penis and two testicles. And the cure for both men and women is to cut off the fused genitals and heal them as with other wounds; but for those men who urinate through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
of the tendon sheath
A swelling is attached to the nail, which is too ugly to look at; some women have it as large as a hand, and that is its growth. It is necessary to remove the excess of the swelling with your hand or with tweezers, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, so that there is no bleeding, then let it heal without further intervention until it is healed; and at another growth that arises at the mouth of the nail, and apply it, and perhaps it will come out, and it resembles a cow's udder, and for this reason they called it in ancient times "cow disease". It is necessary to remove it, as we have said of the swelling, and cure it until it is healed.
Of erratics (roaming joint dislocations)
An erratic condition arises when the nature of a woman is not fully developed, or if it is underdeveloped; this can be natural at birth or caused by an illness. It may also result from a growth or a subtle and fine abscess within the nail bed, on the sides, or underneath, causing obstruction that prevents conception, childbirth, and even menstruation. The recognition of this condition is through observation by a skilled midwife. If the blockage is visible, use your fingers or a probe to locate it. If the abscess is subtle and located near the two lips (labia), act quickly; place your index fingers together and have the woman lie on her back with legs spread apart. Then, stretch the area widely so that the subtle growth is exposed, and carefully insert your fingers above it. Next, take a piece of wool, moisten it with oil, and place it on top. Have the woman lie with a man daily to prevent adhesion. If the abscess is hard and thick, you must remove it using a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. If the blockage is due to fleshy growth, use tweezers to lift and cut it; ensure that you have hemostatic medications like alum, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg white, and place them on a wide wooden board so that the wound does not close up. Then, provide a tent of dry linen and let it heal for an extended period. When fleshy growth appears in the nail bed, remove it using this method if there is no swelling or inflammation. If there is an enlarged swelling in the nail bed, do not attempt to cut into it.
of hemorrhoids
Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that are not usually visible and, when hemorrhoids become old, they turn into nodes (thelul). And we have mentioned in the division their similarities, signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment. That is, both hemorrhoids and nodes (thelul), when deeply embedded in flesh and not perceptible to touch, are not curable by surgery. Those which are at the opening of the anus can be felt and are treatable. Therefore, it is necessary to place the woman in a cold house, then pull out the hemorrhoids with pincers, cutting them at their roots, then sprinkling medicines that constrict blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then let her feet touch the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, place her in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galls and similar things, and take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster on her back. And if it stops (the bleeding), it is good. If not, apply blistering cupping glasses to the back and breasts without breaking them; then take wool, soak it in plantain juice or agrimony juice with old wine, and heat it on the affected area. And when the abscess subsides, cure the area with ointment until it heals; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a hard knob, so it should be covered as I have said for the node (thelul); and then cure it until it heals.
of abscesses of the anus
There are many types of abscesses that can occur in the anus, such as chancre, abscesses filled with pus, herpes, ulcers, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, among other diseases which I have mentioned in the division. It is necessary for me to discuss here the hot abscess that occurs in the anus, which is not one of those that are incised with a knife. And if you want to know the work of surgery, look and see if the abscess is hard at the beginning of its appearance, full of heat and fever, and becoming red if it can be seen. Then do not rush to pierce, but let it mature until the pain subsides; and then make the patient sit on a small seat, and have two small stools for him to lean on, and place his back against the wall and press his legs against the outside of the leg; and spread his thighs, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a strong ligament. Then place a basin at his right side, and prepare the instrument used to open the anus, which will come later in the form; and it is necessary when you are about to insert this instrument that you pierce the root first to determine the depth of the anus, so that what enters inside does not go deeper than it should, and does not wound the patient. And if the instrument is too large, then cover the depth of the anus with rags, so that the instrument does not harm it. And it is necessary for him to place the tip of the instrument above, and hold the instrument. And when the abscess opens and is incised by hand, it should be covered at its base with a small piece of linen; and once the pus has drained, then put in the wound wet bandages soaked in rose oil or dry green oil; and place the bandage deep within the anus, and place over the anus and above it clean wool soaked in water or mallow cooked in water. Then cure it after two days with a suitable ointment until it heals; and sometimes the anus and wound are cleaned by enema of water and honey, and then boiled roots of lilies and aristolochia longa; and then return to the ointment. And if the wound is closed in the anus, then be careful not to burn with a knife, but cure it as we have said in the division.
of childbirth
It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the natural shape and signs of childbirth, and one such sign is when you see the woman bearing down low and having a desire to smell something; this means that the child is eager to come out; therefore, know that this birth is in accordance with nature, and the baby's position is beneath its head, and the umbilical cord is with it. And when you see these signs, then gently press on her belly so that the baby comes out quickly, for once it descends onto its head, the umbilical cord will come with it, and the afterbirth will be expelled from the mother's body through a proper cleansing. But if it comes out any other way, then it is not natural. For instance, sometimes the baby comes out on its feet, or outside of the body, or hands, or it comes out belly-first, or it turns around and gets stuck on its neck, or in other bad positions. Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and clever in these matters, and to be wary of error and deception, and I will show you all of the different positions and how to assist with them.
If the baby comes out headfirst in the natural position and the woman is having a difficult childbirth, and she has weak strength, then make her sit on a stool or have other women hold her. Apply oil or fenugreek that has been heated to her genital area, and then insert the small spatula (the shape of which is described later) with your fingers between her thighs.[1](https://note.meadhbhhandley.com/note/W6XH5f9gRJjbx4qzBQvgPA#_ftn1) and cut the umbilical cord, leaving enough space for the moisture that is inside it to come out; then press on the woman's belly until the baby comes down. If it does not come down, administer a suppository made of fenugreek with oil of sesame to the woman, then have her take a medicine that will make her sneeze and pinch her nose for an hour. The baby should now come out.

of the fistula of the bottom (anus) Fistulas that come from below the anus are swelling and growth that come next to the anus or within a span of two parts (inches).

Arrows
Arrows come in various forms, according to their likenesses and according to the parts of the body where they land.
The varieties of arrows are such that there are those with large points, small ones, barbed and unbarbed. and of those which have two corners, and of those which have tongues, and of those which have fragments; and that which falls in a limb does so in two ways: when it falls in the principal part,
such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.[Reference(s): When it falls in one of the places of these members and signs of death that I will tell you appear to you:[Reference(s): then you must be careful about extracting this arrow, for death often follows in many ways. and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
And the signs of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the suture above the brain is torn. are when there is a scotoma (visual field defect), numbness and vertigo in the eyes, eye inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile. and sometimes bleeding from the nose or ears; and perhaps they lose speech and voice;[ST1] \*St1: "per aventure" is an old French expression meaning "perhaps" or "maybe". and there is discharge from the wound that looks like white matter similar to dough, and also discharge that resembles bruised flesh.
And if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treating and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
The signs of an arrow when it falls near or in the heart are: it is close to the left breast, and it feels as if it is stuck in something hard, not hollow. And perhaps the arrow moves like the pulse, and black blood comes out, and there is cold shivering and cold sweat, and fainting. Then know for certain that death is imminent.[Interestingly, medieval medical texts were not far off in their descriptions of the symptoms of an arrow wound to the heart. Some of the symptoms described here, such as cold sweat and fainting, are still associated with severe shock or internal bleeding today. However, it is important to note that these symptoms do not necessarily indicate that death is imminent. Modern medical care would focus on controlling bleeding, administering fluids and medications to maintain blood pressure and organ function, and possibly surgical intervention. In medieval times, without access to modern medical technology and treatments, a wound to the heart was indeed likely to be fatal.]

Cupping glasses are made of horns, or of tin, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
And this cupping which is without striking is done in two ways: either with all heat, or without heat;[
and two others are on either side of the neck; and the cupping glass under the chin; and the cupping glass on both shoulders; and the cupping glass on the hips; and the cupping glasses between both arms; and the cupping glasses on both legs; And the cups of the two ankles; and the cupping does not draw blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh.

This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Know, dear son, that foolish doctors throw away this chapter, for they never look at any of the ancient books or read letters (of them).
And because of this, the knowledge is strange in our land, for I never found any good one (doctor) who knows it.
And I know nothing of it, except for the knowledge from ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have mastered the subject, and by experience, and by being accustomed to it in my life.
And I have described for you in this chapter what it contains, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, just as I did in these two chapters before.
Therefore, it is appropriate in the prologue of this book that we list the summaries of the teachings and the chapters where the wise person concentrates their understanding and stays true to the truth, so that those who have been tested may know and learn this noble art and then teach it to others.
I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing occurs in someone, then you must hurry to heal the patient from both sides if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of the body, children, or the elderly;
or if the season is not extremely hot or very cold, and you should eat cool foods, such as cold meats like chicken and rabbit, and not drink wine, nor eat any greasy meats, and do not fill yourself with too much food that fills the veins with blood, until there is no doubt of a hot abscess or swelling of matter in the limb; then let the patient return to their usual regimen.
And when the fractured bone begins to restore itself, then the patient should be nourished with foods that promote substantial nourishment, or that are viscous, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and meat from the head, feet, and entrails of animals, eggs, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things. For through proper care, deformities and fractures are healed more quickly.
And know that the bones of the old and infirm cannot heal or knit together properly according to their nature due to the weakness of their limbs, nor can those who are too young, such as the bones of small children;
but do not worry, set a large peg on the broken bone which pulls and brings the limb together until it heals as before; and do not disturb its work, and therefore it must be nourished with rich foods, as we have said.
And know that fractures are diverse and varied in many ways.
For a break in the skull is different from a break in the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fracture. For there is a break that tends to go towards the groin, and another that goes towards the sharp point, like the cut of a pen's nib for writing.
For there is a break that tends to go towards the groin, and another that goes towards the sharp point, like the cut of a pen's nib for writing. And if there is a break with a wound, and a break is just a small fissure.

and let the inflammation of the limb rest, and remove the pain, then gently restart the ligature, and a little emplaster, and do not constrict it as much as before; and gently until it is healed.
And if you see that an abscess is red, swollen, painful, and has opened completely, and you need emplaster and bandages, then reapply it as you did in the beginning.
And if no improvement is seen in the limb after the treatments we have mentioned, then do not release it before 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days, and sometimes leave it for 20 days, depending on what is observed, until the break heals and the joining of flesh begins.
then bind it more tightly than before and the flesh will fatten, as I said earlier; and if you see that the place is drying out more than necessary, know that there can be no healing. boil the joint in hot water each time you release it, every third day, and loosen the ligament a little;
by this work, therefore, the blood flow to the limb is cut off and quickly corrects what foolish doctors do when they incorrectly restore the limb: it is wrong, and I see no other solution than to leave it alone and work on it correctly.
"of the different ways of fracture" There are many types of fractures, with various shapes and distinct causes;
because there are fractures caused by sword blows, and the collarbone separates the entire bone down to the shaft that is underneath the bone, just like an axe or stick would do; therefore, this type of fracture is called "haichure".
Where the sword cuts the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
And if there is a hidden impact, or a split from a stone or a fall on a stone, or from other similar causes.
And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the membrane beneath the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is large or small.[Note: The word "toile" here refers to a membrane or tissue under the skin or bone.]
And if there is a wound that is embedded in the bone as thin as a hair, and the split is small, and for this reason it is called this type of fracture "hairline".[Note: The word "chevous" here means hairs or very fine strands.][Stylistic note: I have used the spelling "fracture" instead of the original "brisure" to maintain consistency in terminology.]
And if the wound is made by striking with a stone or by falling, and it drives a piece of bone inward, and the site appears like blisters that blacksmiths get when they hammer on cauldrons, and stones enter inside.
And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their head, such as the bones of a child;
And this occurs in all these types of fractures where small pieces are separated, such as splinters; and I will speak on that later.
And we know all types of fractures by the withdrawal (or traction) on them, and through investigation using probes, and by the corrupt flesh that is on top (of the wound).
The appearance of a fracture (resembling hair) is recognized by this: when the bone is uncovered and rubbed against, the fracture appears black.
In the treatment of a fracture, be aware of the patient's condition and if you see any adverse symptoms, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, swelling, paleness, feverishness, eyes becoming exserted and red, and other similar signs in various dispositions, then it cannot be healed without a doubt.
And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for recovery, then begin the cure.
And when the wounded person comes to you first, and it is winter, you should remove the bone within the fourteenth day at the latest that you can.
And if it is in the summer, you should quickly remove the bone within the seventh day, so that the tissue underneath the bone does not become corrupt and the accidents that we have mentioned do not occur.
And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, you must split open the affected part in this way: that is, take hold of the head of the wounded person and expose the bone as much as you can, and as gently as possible on the surface of the wound
And if bleeding occurs when the bone is exposed or an abscess arises, use what is necessary and fill the wound with cloths soaked in rose oil and let the wound rest until the abscess has subsided, and you are assured of proper blood flow; then begin around the bone to remove [the pus], and this is done in two ways: one way is to make a narrow incision in front, and its shape is:
And then make another incision that is larger than the first one.
And the second way is to have multiple incisions of varying sizes, some narrow and others wide, with sharp points, and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.[In this context, "head" refers to the pus-filled abscess or swelling that needs to be drained. The text advises making multiple incisions of different sizes and shapes, some narrow and others wide, with sharp points, and made of iron, and to do so carefully and skillfully so as not to injure the surrounding tissue.]
And if the bone is hard and protruding, then you must make incisions around it so as to provide openings for drainage, but not so deep that they penetrate beyond the bone of the abscess; and above the point of each incision there should be a margin or a ring that prevents the point from penetrating beyond the bone. And you should have several such stoppers, placed in such a way as to cover the entire surface of the bone; this is the shape of the three types of stoppers:
The qualities for drilling around the broken bone are: place a drill on the bone, and turn it towards your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then move the drill a bit further, and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone between the holes with the incisors, doing this as delicately and lightly as you can, until you draw out the bone with your hand or with one of the tools you have such as pincers; and take care not to touch the brain or the skull.
And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary to smooth the sharpness that remains of the bone with another tool similar to an incisor, but it should be thinner and more delicate than the other incisors.
And if there remains any small bones or scales, remove them lightly with one of the tools; then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
And the other method of work is what Galen describes, which is safer and he praised it highly; and this is his statement: It is necessary, firstly, that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break is clearly visible. So that once you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lenticular scalpel, of which this is the shape:
And do not saw from one side, but rather make two cuts on either side so that the cutting edge faces the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet so that you lightly cut through the bone all around, taking great care of the cloth beneath.
If it is attached to the bone, remove it carefully, for it can be removed without harm and without fear.
And if the break in the bone does not penetrate through to the cloth, but rather it is only cut from above and there are small fragments, then you must smooth over that roughness and remove the splinters with a fine razor of which you should have various quantities, so as to make the most suitable adjustments according to the work and shape of the break in each location.
If the king before large razors, and afterward with finer ones, and do not stop until it is well done.
But the king (in every other haircut and fine breakage), it is necessary that you adjust according to its growth; and this is not an obvious matter even for one who has studied this art.
And if the abscess is exposed, then it is necessary to take a linen cloth of appropriate size for the wound, soak it in rose oil and place it on top of the wound. Next, take another cloth, doubled in two or three layers, soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth. Do this as gently as possible, taking care not to harm the abscess. Then apply a bandage over it without tightening too much, just enough to hold the wound closed.[0]
And leave it like this for one or two days until the abscess has subsided. Then loosen the bandage and apply medicinal herbs such as lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things. Make a powder of these ingredients and sprinkle it on the wound. Apply other mild medicines without causing biting pain.
And see that the wound is always clean, that you do not leave any pus, and do not allow any worms to gather, because when worms gather on the cloth of the brain, they will crawl and irritate, and this will cause great harm to the patient; for when something biting is placed on the siphac (a piece of bone in the skull), it will bite through from above.
Take heed then, if any bad accident should befall the patient, as we have said, it is to be doubted with doubt.
And if no other cause for the complication arises but from the medicine that has been applied, and it has such power, then you should take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and mix them with one cloth, and place it on the siphac (a piece of bone in the skull). Then treat the complication with various treatments until it is healed.
Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, either one alone, as there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, it only swells or twists, and then heals.
And if one of the two parts is broken, you should insert your little finger or the hole of the nose, and align the break inside your index finger, and with your thumb on the outside, until the nose regains its natural shape. And do this gently, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and your finger cannot reach it, then you should use a rod about as thick as a finger to align it.[References (in French)](https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k56390q/f76.item)
And if the break is in two parts, do the same and hurry to restore it on the first day if you can.[References (in French)](https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k56390q/f76.item)
if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has calmed down, then apply to the wound of the broken part a linen cloth dipped in wine.
and put one (cloth) on the other side if the break is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the wounds of the nose.
And some physicians say that one should moisten the bandages with butter and change them every day. But it does not seem good to me; rather, they should be moistened with a preparation of egg yolk and powdered mill; then leave the bandage until the bone is healed and the cartilage hardened.
And sometimes goose feathers are put into the nose instead of bandages, and a soft cloth is wrapped around it, and the patient holds it in place, and breathes through it; do as you please.[ fight Club reference? :) ]
And if an abscess comes to the nose while you are working on it, put a wax seal or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a piece of diachylon (sticky plaster) on it.[Note: Diachylon is a medical term for a plaster that can be sticked to the skin and was used as a drug delivery system. It's like a medicated band-aid.]
And if abscesses do not appear, apply an external plaster, made of chamomile flour, and powdered incense, mixed with egg white, then put light wicks on it, but do not bind it.
And if the fracture of the nail is small and it is broken into many pieces, then extract it with appropriate instruments, then sew up the wound, and cure it from harmful things such as dirt and pus, using appropriate plasters and ointments for this.
And if there is no wound inside the nail, then cure it with bandages and place splints of wood until it heals.
about the fracture of the jawbone
When the lower jaw is dislocated, and there is no wound above it, and the fracture is only displaced, and not broken in two, except for a chip inside, it can be easily recognized.
If the fracture is on the right side, you should put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left side of the jaw, you should insert your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the fracture back into place, and align it with the other hand from the outside.
And if the jaw fracture is separated into two parts, you must apply extension to both parts until they are aligned.
If movement of the teeth or fractures occur, bind them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then apply a cerate to the broken jaw and place a double bandage over it. Place a large well-made star-shaped piece or a piece of leather of equal size, length, and width on top of the bandage, securing it as high as possible, and command the patient to rest and eat light foods.[Comments: The text recommends using precious metals such as gold or silver for binding fractured teeth, which is consistent with the medical practices of the time where expensive materials were often used in medical treatments. Cerate refers to a medicinal plaster or salve.]
And if you see the figure changing, unbind it on the third day, and then realign what has become misaligned; and apply a plaster on top, with powder from the mill and plenty of egg or chickpea flour, after removing the wax; and place light linen on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out, and the patient's condition does not worsen, leave it on until it heals; it often heals in three weeks.
And if an abscess comes, use what we have said many times.
And if there is a fracture and wound together, see if any piece of bone has been removed; it is necessary to delicately remove it with the appropriate instruments.[« »]
And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire as needed.
And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then stitch the wound, if it is large, and apply one of suitable poultices for healing flesh until it has healed.

of the shoulder fracture.

Here is the translation of the original Old French text you provided:
Sometimes there occurs a fracture of the neck bones, and it rarely bends; and also in the spine of the back. And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, pay attention if you see their hands weakened, swollen, and numb, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that they are mortally injured in many ways, but if they can move them and feel when they are strained and poked, know that the joints of the bone are safe, and that the patient will be cured if treated.
And if a similar thing happens in the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, pay attention if their feet are weak, and if there are symptoms in their hands that are similar, and on their back there is a swelling and discharge without voluntary movement; and when it is pressed on their stomach, there is discharge without voluntary movement. And when they try to sit up while lying on their back, they cannot. Know that they are mortally injured: do not labor in their cure.
And if these symptoms do not occur, then the condition is less severe.
And the treatment is that you should check if there is a hot abscess, and if there is, place on it rose oil or egg yolk oil, until it calms down; then apply one of the healing and drying ointments, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on the side where they feel pain, until they are healed. And if any bone gets dislocated, it should be covered on the chest; and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a stitch, then cure it with an ointment that draws out flesh, until it heals; and if the hole of the bone is broken, which is called the "hole of the cow", insert your left hand pocket, and place it evenly with your other hand to your power, then apply the ointment and bandage if necessary; then bind it, and if there is a dislocated bone, push on it, remove it, and cure the wound until it heals.
"about the fracture of the thigh bone" (femur)
It rarely happens that the thigh bone is broken, and if it does happen, it is only slightly narrowed at the end; it bends long, and deviates to the side, causing pain to the patient in the area, swelling, and deformity of the fractured part.
And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand on top, so that you are above the break; and know what the break and its shape is; and if the break is at the head only, then align that break equally, so that it is in its natural shape.
And if the break is long, or it slopes inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach, so that you can align the restoration of that break. And when you have aligned it equally, then apply the poultice and place a wooden or bone splint on top, holding the break in place so that it does not move, and apply a bandage underneath the ribs, until they are properly aligned.[FAQ]
And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
And if abscesses come in its place, do not touch it until the abscesses have calmed down, and apply what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as is necessary, if there is no adverse accident; and this is the method.
Of the break of the shoulder.
The shoulder joint is what is between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored in one of two ways: one of which is to take a rod of medium size, according to this shape:
And bind the two shoulders with two bandages and pull them up, and place the patient on a seat; then throw his broken arm over the rod, until it reaches the armpit and is in the middle of a bow-shaped piece of wood; then hang it over some heavy object or the attendant pulls it down; then put the surgeon's hands together around the break, until the break returns to its proper place.
And the other manner is to place the patient on a stretcher, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants to hold with one's hands what is above the break, and the other holds below all one tendon, and each pulls to their side.
And if you see that the extraction needs to be stronger, then tighten one tendon below the break, and above it, and have each assistant pull to their side. And if the break is close to the top of the shoulder, then you must place one tendon in the middle below the socket, and another towards the edge, below the break; and do the same if the break is toward the edge. Place a tendon lightly, without effort, just enough so that the break is aligned with its place, and the socket; then align the break as it should be, and tighten it, if there is no sign of abscesses.
And if an abscess appears, then do not tighten it for seven days, and apply a wet linen cloth in vinegar and rose oil, until the abscess subsides; then tighten it, and the manner of tightening is that you put the poultice on the break, then place the arm on the shoulder or chest; and wrap the bandage, and tighten it on the stretcher, and on the arm, so that the arm remains straight, if nothing hinders it, or if the bone is not broken.
And if you are unsure whether the bone is broken, then use splints and place a wider and stronger splint over the break, with a space of two fingers between each splint, and make each splint large enough to pass over the break by three fingers on each side; then tighten it with splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, more tightly and less evenly.
And if you see the swelling and tightening, as we have said, at the time you reset the broken member, and you doubt a hot abscess, then let it be bound up until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine the binding every three days to see if itching, inflammation, or discharge comes to the place, or if circulation cannot reach the member because the binding is too tight. If so, loosen it as we have said.
And if no such accidents occur, then do not unbind it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; and place a cushion full of evenly spread wool underneath the affected area, and check every hour of the day and night to see that the shape of the broken member does not change, or if the binding has become too loose; then adjust it by the power of medicine, and give them food as we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is initially fine; and when they begin to recover, the food should be coarse. It is customary for the affected area and leg to regain their normal state in 40 days; and then one should unbind it and administer baths and medicinal ointments to direct the place towards healing. And if the stricture is severe and embedded, then it should be left unbound for one day or two months.
The text does not provide a new sentence in English, it just specifies that the previous instructions were about "the break of the arm" (la brisure du bras). Here is the previous translation again:
The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "radius" and the "ulna," with one being smaller and the other being larger. The smaller one is located above, and it is the one that follows the thumb; while the larger one is located below, near the little finger. It may happen that only the large radius bone breaks, or only the small ulna bone, or both at once.
When the small bones are broken, the restoration and healing is easy; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is difficult and more severe than when they are both broken together. If it is only the small bone that is broken, then it should be lightly stretched and aligned.
And if it is the large bone, then it must be stretched more forcefully; and it should be placed over a cushion, and the little finger of the hand should be held higher than the others, and the small toes lower than the others, and have the patient lie crosswise on it, with a cushion before them so that they do not suffer any labor. Then the assistant extends the patient's arm below at their side, or with a strap, and another assistant above. And then the doctor aligns it evenly, according to its best form.
And if the break is in pieces, then place each piece in its place, and if there is any piece that is torn and pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make an incision above and remove it, as we have said before.
And if there is a wound with the break, I have spoken of this in a separate chapter; then take care of the treatment.
And if in the beginning of the restoration pustules occur, then place a piece of lard cloth made of rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard or too soft; and gently bind a cloth over it, until the pustules have calmed down. And then remove the lard cloth, and apply the plaster of the powder from the mill with plenty of egg, then place the stylets, and let the stylet of the breakage be stronger and slightly larger than the others; and know that it should have six stylets or branches in several dispositions: whether the breaker is in one of the bones, or in two; and bind more above the breakage than any other part, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are above the breakage be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread, with which it is bound, be of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And wrap the member and the bandage after several days. And if any bad accidents come to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then it is necessary to rinse the member with warm water until the itching has calmed down; and let the member not rest tightly. And then begin binding again, and if the bandages are softened and the bones disjoined, and similar things, then address them.
And if you notice that the blood flow cannot come to the member because it is too tight, then you must loosen it slightly and leave it like that for several days until the blood flows again, and then bind it again.[x](https://www.memrise.com/learn/english/course/old-french/phrase/et-se-prend-warde-se-li-norrissemens-ne-puet-venir-au-member-por-ceu-quil-est-trop-estrois-si-covient-que-tu-lamollisses-i-poc-et-laisse-ensi-aucuns-jors-tant-que-li-norrissemens-i-corre-et-puis-lestrain/)
And if none of the things we have mentioned do not come to the patient, then do not release it until after 20 days or so; then let him wash his hands at his neck and let his neck be even, and watch for movement and swelling, and let him sleep on his back. And know that this breakage is restored in 30 or 35 days, and perhaps in 20 days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
of the broken hand
Know that breaks in the back of the hand and at the knuckles often occur, but it is usually a sprain that happens many times.
And when the palm of the hand is broken or sprained, then the patient should sit cross-legged and sit upright in front of them; then place their hand on a spread out cloth, and the assistant straightens the broken bones and aligns them properly until they are well joined; and apply the dressing and bandages, unless there are abscesses, then place a splint according to the size of the location; and wrap it in a linen cloth.
And if the break is on the outer side around the belly of the palm, then make a cushion of cloth, and instruct the patient to press it against their broken palm; and then bind it with a long bandage, and let the splint be made of wood as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it as needed.
And if the break is on the outside, then you should place a splint on top of it, and another underneath in the palm of the hand, so that the hand is open and straight; then bind it around the entire hand, and fasten the bandage between the fingers.[(\*](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/tout_entor) ")).
And if the bone setter comes to one of our fingers, if it is crooked, place it evenly as it should be; and bind it with the sole (of a foot), and if you see fit, place a straight small stake to raise the fracture, and do not move it; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, place it evenly, and bind it with the healthy finger that is after; or tie them all together, so that moving (the bandage) is useful, or place a stake on it, like on a crooked finger; and take care in the restoration and placement of hot abscesses, and heal those who come to it, as I have said.
Of the broken thigh.
The thigh bone is often broken, and it is easily visible when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration consists of tying one ligature above the fracture, and another below. And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends their ligature evenly to their part; and that is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
And if the fracture is near the hip root, then let one of the ligaments be towards the wrist, and the other ligament below the fracture. And similarly if it is close to the knee, and then let the ligament be next to the knee, and let the extension be downwards; then let the surgeon place the bone even with his two hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then put on the poultice and the bandage, if pus does not appear.
And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down first and then return to your work and care; the ligature is done in such a way. It is necessary that you wrap over the fracture a hard bandage doubled in two or three layers, leaving excess material; then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, next to the knee below, and let the end of the thread come to the top; then wrap back over the leg and thigh the bandage, then place splints on the fracture and one splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the gap between the thigh and the leg with soft cloths to make the tension even, then begin to tie firmly three or four turns over the fracture; and as you go further up from the fracture, tighten less; then pay attention to the two ends of the thread that you put between the thigh and the leg, and tie three splints that are above, then go back down to the bottom end of the thread until you come next to the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, as long as there is no abscess or swelling or any other symptom.
And if there is a wound, untie it and treat what comes out, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, they should be removed if possible; and if not, then the wound must be opened wider and the fragments extracted; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
And sometimes the hip is broken so that steel pins are put in, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, the patient does not fare well in such a restoration.
And know that the hip is restored in 3 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the differences in constitutions.
of the groove of the knee
Know that there are few fractures in the groove of the knee, but it often dislocates. And if it breaks, it is only a split or a hole, and this happens with all wounds, both with and without wounds, and this can be felt clearly.
And the restoration is such that you put evenly what is dislocated at its two ends, until it can be moved as a whole; then apply the poultice and place a round bandage if needed, and bind it appropriately. Then, consider all the precautions that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar ones; and for each symptom, do what is necessary until it is healed.

Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
When a dislocation occurs, one must immediately attempt to correct it.
For if one delays, the area will swell and it may be difficult to reset; therefore, it is not advisable to move it when it is swollen, as this can cause vomiting and other pains in many cases.
Nevertheless, when this occurs, have the patient bled, then wait until the swelling has subsided. Then apply warm water and oil to the affected limb before gently resetting it. Treat each limb as it returns to its proper place.[In medieval medicine, bloodletting was a common treatment for many ailments, including inflammation. The heat of the water and oil would have been soothing and helped to relax muscles, making it easier to reset the dislocation. The phrase "cure chescun membre" means that each limb should be treated as it returns to its proper place.]
And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the joints from the head to the feet.

And the signs of this are that excretions leave the body involuntarily and cannot be held in, and often certain limbs become weakened, or both thighs or both arms or one.[](Note: The Old French text seems to have some errors or omissions as it is written. And often, the small of the back moves in four ways; the one that moves at the back is called "gilbositez".[note: The Old French term "gilbositez" does not have a clear modern equivalent. It may refer to a specific type of spinal deformity or injury, but its exact meaning is uncertain.]
The treatment is to determine if "gilbositez" has been present since childhood; if so, there is no cure or complete healing.
And this which comes from falling or being struck or similar things, the ancient methods of cures said in grand words, there is not always great benefit in all of them;
but I have abbreviated it according to my intention and have created instruments in diverse ways.
I say that in the gelbiness (inflammation) that comes at the front of the breast, there is no remedy or health.
And also this which comes directly in the two ribs (lateral sides of the chest), cannot be cured unless it is specifically that which comes at the back, as I say.
And it is necessary that the patient be stretched out on his back evenly and have support beneath him so that they do not injure themselves.
then stick a stake into the ground deeply, and another by the patient's feet, and tie a ligament under the soles of the patient's feet, and another at the thighs, and at the knees;
and two assistants know the bindings, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes;
and let them be tightly bound, the stakes as we have said, and the physician places his palms firmly on the spine until it heals.[Note: I'm assuming "espinee" refers to the affected body part that needs healing. The word can mean "spine", but in this context, it may refer to a dislocated joint or bone.]
And if it does not heal with this treatment, take a plank of three arms length, curved on the underside, and let the patient lie on their side, then place the middle of the plank on the affected area (I assume "l'espinee" refers to the back in this context), and position the head of the plank under the patient's side. and let the physician place his feet on the other end of the plank, pressing firmly until it returns to its proper position; and if necessary, use a device that can be turned by hand (perhaps some kind of mechanical device) to apply more pressure.
And insert two sticks in the head of the patient, one on each arm, and have a palm's space between each stick, both above and below.
And have each stick have one hole, where the rope can pass through, and securely fasten the sticks in the ground so that they do not move; and between every two sticks, have a turning stick, on which the ropes turn, and have two small sticks of one palm's length between the two turning sticks, to turn the turning stick.
And then tie the rope between the ashes to the turning stick towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other turning stick, and each of the assistants turns their turning stick fully around, and the master puts the needle in evenly as we have said.
And when it is even, apply a desiccative plaster with an abundance of egg, and then the wicks, and then a piece of wood three fingers long from a tablet that covers the area of gout and the healthy part of the shoulder blade, then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and treat the patient delicately until they are healed.
And if something happens at the end of the healing process, such medical drugs that soften and soothe, with the starstone we mentioned earlier; and sometimes a piece of lead is administered.
And sometimes an appearance occurs on the back spondylus of the back, and it is thought to be a dislocation; but it is the bone that protrudes, for which one should not assume: perhaps it would bring about death.
of hip dislocations
Know that the hip joint and shoulder joint only come out of place by dislocations, and not in the same way as other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated in four ways: from within and without, and from the front and back; and more so from within than elsewhere, and slightly from the front and back.
And the recognition of an internal dislocation is that when the affected leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee appears higher than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee by the fire. and is the place that is next to inflamed abscesses due to the fact that the hip's head moves there.
And the sign of this person, for whom it comes too late, is that these symptoms are contrary to those before.
And the sign of this person, for whom it comes too early, is that they stretch their leg well according to its completion; nevertheless, they do not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants them to walk, they cannot move forward, and they retain their urine, and their ankle swells, and when they walk, they step on their heel.
And the sign of this person, for whom it happens later, is that they cannot stretch or bend their knee, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is swollen, and the hip's head is in the place below the ribs.[
The reduction of this similar type of dislocation is as follows: you should examine whether the dislocation is old and remains in its position, in which case there is no need for treatment and one should not be overconfident.
And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four types of dislocations, you should quickly set the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other cure is needed.
And if it does not return in this way, you should prepare one strong minister, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or with one ligament tied above the knee; and have another minister extend his hand in such a way that he pushes his hands beneath the patient's armpits, then bind him with a gentle ligament on the thigh, and one holds the end of the ligament.[5 lines not shown as they are repeated from previous translations]
and pull upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground and remains hanging.[5 lines not shown as they are repeated from previous translations]
This manner of stretching is common to four similar things, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
If not, one must attend to its likeness. When the dislocation is on the side, you should turn the patient onto their healthy side, then place the bandage on the root of the thigh and the area beneath the groin, then pull the bandage up towards the groin and towards the shoulder;
then take another person to hold the patient's arms, and embrace the affected thigh with a large bandage and stretch it out forcefully; it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
And if you cannot secure it in this manner as we have said, then you must bind the patient's two feet together with a strong soft ligament at the heels and at the knees, and keep the affected leg extended two fingers' width more than the other;
and let them hang from the head of a beam, and be two arms' length from the ground; then command one assistant to embrace the thigh and have another assistant hanging with the patient, who will forcefully embrace the thigh, for now the joint will return quickly.
And when the dislocation is outside, let the patient lie down, as we have said in the one who has gout, and tighten a ligament on the sick leg properly, and also on the foot.
then place two splints, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert one splint between the patient's thighs in the shape of [the letter] N. and wrap it with damp cloths to prevent injury to the patient, then each assistant stretches out towards him, and the surgeon places his hand equal to the dislocation.
If it returns (to its proper position), that is good. If not, place the patient on a table and press as we have said in gout, and let the patient lie on his healthy side.
And when the dislocation is in front, you must quickly stretch out the sick leg as I have said, and the surgeon should take care to be over the affected ankle, then press with his other hand and pull down towards the knee.
And if the dislocation is outward, it should not be stretched downward, nor lifted upward, but instead, it should be in the same position as if the swelling is dislocated outward, as we have said about lying on two inflamed legs. And let it be face down, and the bandages extended as we have said before, and one should press on the joint against the table.
And it will be ready when the patient extends their legs and they are even; then adjust the thighs, apply the poultice, and bind it with a bandage so that the swelling does not move.[Answer 10:
And let it rest for three or four days, then loosen it and apply the poultice as before, and if you see that they are even, bind it as previously described and leave it for three days; then loosen it and make the patient walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
of the dislocation of the knee
The knee dislocates in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
And the sign is that you tell the patient to bend their leg to their hip, and if it does not reach, know that it is dislocated.
And the restoration of all [dislocations] is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg if they can, and place your back to their face, and put their foot on top of your feet.
then take their knee in your palms, and pull it towards you between your arms, then strongly bend the two sides of the knee; and have another assistant stretch out their leg until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that they can easily bend their leg to their hip.
and put the poultice on, and heat up the leg to the thigh, and bind the limbs together firmly for three or four days, then loosen it; and the patient should not move at all until the limb is healed.
And if the limb is not healthy yet, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of inflammation, until it is healed.
for ankle dislocation[jj](/):
The ankle can sometimes be dislocated, both inside and outside.
And the signs of this are that the ankle is swollen, and it tends to move towards the side where it is dislocated.
the setting [of the dislocation] is easy, and it should be gently stretched with his hands when he is moved slightly.
And when it has been completely dislocated, you should make the patient sit upright and have one assistant hold him by the leg, above the ankle.
then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then do it two more times, then stretch it upwards and forcefully push the foot up.[ br /]
and do this two times, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it goes back into place, that's good; if not, then start the process over again, because it will go back into place.[br /]
If it cannot be put back in place that way, then make the patient lie down on their back on the ground, and firmly plant a stake in the ground between their legs and wrap cloth around it so that it does not hurt the patient.
then have the minister bend the thigh, and another minister stretch the foot with their hands or with a ligament, that they tie to the neck of the foot; then have each minister stretch (the limb) evenly, and the bandage should be placed again between the patient's thighs to support the patient as they are stretched.
then have the surgeon set the dislocation with their hands, and another minister hold the healthy leg down below, and the dislocation will quickly return (to its proper place).
And when it is in place, apply the plaster and bandages strongly, and bind the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle in the back, so that the ligament is not too tight.
then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligament weakens, rebind it; then unbind it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days. and if it goes before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
And if abscesses come, you should soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
of the hands
When the hands are dislocated, they should be stretched out nicely without effort, and this is an easy thing to do.
And if the dislocation is in any node of the back or leg, you should make the patient sit on a flat surface or on two tables in a straight position. Place your foot on the part where the joints are exposed, then press firmly with your foot until it goes back into place.[
and when it is even, and there is nothing visible, place a two-footed table under the sole of the foot, then apply strong pressure and leave it for three days, then loosen it; and let it rest until it is healed.
of wound and dislocation together
When a wound accompanies the dislocation, and one wishes to heal it, it often happens that the patient dies.
and do not be at all presumptuous in the treatment if you are not skilled in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, not hasty.
And begin with soothing treatments for an inflamed abscess and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope of health. and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the abscess comes to a head;
and when the limb is in its place, administer warming compresses for the abscess, and treat the wound as appropriate with drying ointments;
and if there is a fracture along with the dislocation and broken small bones, then set them and do as we have said in simple illnesses;[NOTE: I'm assuming "maladies simples" refers to another section of the text that discusses treating simple illnesses or injuries.]
and take care not to enter the path of fear, as I have said, for it is up to your Creator how long you live, and for the safety of your tools and body. Amen.
